## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (solid mechanics / materials science)
**Analysis**: With sigma as stress, epsilon as strain, and T as temperature, the task most naturally fits constitutive (stress–strain) laws for solids where stiffness, yield, and hardening/softening depend on temperature. Common structures include elastic relations with temperature-dependent modulus, thermal-strain offsets, and nonlinear hardening combined with thermal softening.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear elasticity (Hooke): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic stiffness varies approximately linearly with T)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (exponential softening): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (rapid stiffness change with T; typically c1 < 0 for softening)
- Thermoelastic with thermal-strain offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (thermal expansion strain subtracts from mechanical strain)
- Nonlinear elastic (Landau/Murnaghan-type truncation): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon^2 + c2 * epsilon^3 (moderate strain nonlinearity without plasticity)
- Power-law hardening (Hollomon-type): sigma = c0 * (Abs(epsilon) + c1)^c2 * Sign(epsilon) (plastic-like monotone hardening in strain; sign handles tension/compression)
- Ramberg–Osgood-style direct stress form: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon^c2 (elastic + nonlinear hardening contribution)
- Combined hardening with thermal softening (multiplicative): sigma = (c0 + c1 * (Abs(epsilon) + c2)^c3) * exp(c4 * T) * Sign(epsilon) (strain hardening modulated by T)
- Polynomial-in-T thermoelasticity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T^2) * (epsilon - c3 * (T - c4)) (captures curvature in E(T) and thermal strain)
- Yield-like saturation via smooth transition: sigma = c0 * tanh(c1 * epsilon) * exp(c2 * T) (approaches a limiting stress level; temperature shifts scale)
- Thermal softening with normalized temperature gap: sigma = (c0 + c1 * (Abs(epsilon) + c2)^c3) * (1 - c4 * (T - c5)^c6) * Sign(epsilon) (strength drops as T increases toward a critical range)
- Hyperbolic-sine constitutive (Eyring-like stress response shape): sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon) * exp(c2 * T) (nonlinear stress–strain curvature with thermal factor)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic regime identification: sigma approximately proportional to epsilon suggests a dominant linear term; deviations indicate nonlinear elasticity or plasticity terms (powers of epsilon or tanh/asinh shapes).
- Thermal expansion manifests as an intercept shift: an apparent nonzero stress at epsilon = 0 often indicates sigma depends on (epsilon - c * (T - T0)).
- Temperature-dependent stiffness: if slope d(sigma)/d(epsilon) decreases with T, model E(T) with decreasing functions such as c0 + c1 * T (c1 < 0) or exp(c * T) (c < 0).
- Strength/hardening temperature coupling: when higher T reduces stress at the same epsilon, prefer multiplicative softening factors applied to a hardening backbone, e.g., sigma_hard(epsilon) * exp(c * T).
- Rapid softening near a critical temperature: abrupt drop-offs with T are better captured by higher-order (T - c)^n terms inside (1 - ...) factors or by strong exponentials in T.
- Tension–compression symmetry: if the material response is approximately odd in epsilon, include Sign(epsilon) with functions of Abs(epsilon) to enforce antisymmetry while keeping magnitudes positive.
- Curvature changes with strain: increasing tangent modulus with epsilon suggests hardening-like power laws; decreasing tangent modulus suggests saturation forms like tanh/asinh.
- Separability check: if sigma(ε,T) nearly factorizes into f(epsilon) * g(T), multiplicative forms are preferred over fully coupled polynomials.
